window['google_ads']
=
google_ads;




if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Deep_Purple';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"purple,_,deep,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Deep
Purple</b>
are
an
English
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
music">rock</a>
band
formed
in
<a
href="/wiki/Hertford?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hertford">Hertford</a>
in
1968.<sup
id="cite_ref-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
are
considered
to
be
among
the
pioneers
of
<a
href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Heavy
metal
music">heavy
metal</a>
and
modern
<a
href="/wiki/Hard_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hard
rock">hard
rock</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-Wasler_2-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Wasler-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Campbell_3-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Campbell-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
although
their
musical
approach
changed
over
the
years.<sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
Originally
formed
as
a
<a
href="/wiki/Progressive_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Progressive
rock">progressive
rock</a>
band,
the
band's
sound
shifted
to
hard
rock
in
1970.
Deep
Purple,
together
with
<a
href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Led
Zeppelin">Led
Zeppelin</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Sabbath">Black
Sabbath</a>,
have
been
referred
to
as
the
&quot;unholy
trinity
of
British
hard
rock
and
heavy
metal
in
the
early
to
mid-Seventies&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
were
listed
in
the
1975
<a
href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guinness
World
Records"><i>Guinness
Book
of
World
Records</i></a>
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Loudest_band_in_the_world?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Loudest
band
in
the
world">the
globe's
loudest
band</a>&quot;
for
a
1972
concert
at
London's
<a
href="/wiki/Rainbow_Theatre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rainbow
Theatre">Rainbow
Theatre</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Jason_Ankeny_7-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jason_Ankeny-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
have
sold
over
100&nbsp;million
albums
worldwide,<sup
id="cite_ref-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
including
8
million
certified
units
in
the
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
band
has
gone
through
many
line-up
changes
and
an
eight-year
hiatus
(1976–1984).
The
1968–1976
line-ups
are
commonly
labelled
Mark
I,
II,
III
and
IV.<sup
id="cite_ref-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
Their
second
and
most
commercially
successful
line-up
featured
<a
href="/wiki/Ian_Gillan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ian
Gillan">Ian
Gillan</a>
(vocals),
<a
href="/wiki/Jon_Lord?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jon
Lord">Jon
Lord</a>
(organ),
<a
href="/wiki/Roger_Glover?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roger
Glover">Roger
Glover</a>
(bass),
<a
href="/wiki/Ian_Paice?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ian
Paice">Ian
Paice</a>
(drums),
and
<a
href="/wiki/Ritchie_Blackmore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ritchie
Blackmore">Ritchie
Blackmore</a>
(guitar).
This
line-up
was
active
from
1969
to
1973,
and
was
revived
from
1984
to
1989,
and
again
from
1992
to
1993.
The
band
achieved
more
modest
success
in
the
intervening
periods
between
1968
and
1969
with
the
line-up
including
<a
href="/wiki/Rod_Evans?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rod
Evans">Rod
Evans</a>
(vocals)
and
<a
href="/wiki/Nick_Simper?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nick
Simper">Nick
Simper</a>
(bass,
backing
vocals),
between
1974
and
1976
(<a
href="/wiki/Tommy_Bolin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tommy
Bolin">Tommy
Bolin</a>
replacing
Blackmore
in
1975)
with
the
line-up
including
<a
href="/wiki/David_Coverdale?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Coverdale">David
Coverdale</a>
(vocals)
and
<a
href="/wiki/Glenn_Hughes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glenn
Hughes">Glenn
Hughes</a>
(bass,
vocals),
and
between
1989
and
1992
with
the
line-up
including
<a
href="/wiki/Joe_Lynn_Turner?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joe
Lynn
Turner">Joe
Lynn
Turner</a>
(vocals).
The
band's
line-up
(currently
featuring
Ian
Gillan,
and
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Steve_Morse?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Steve
Morse">Steve
Morse</a>
from
1994)
has
been
much
more
stable
in
recent
years,
although
organist
Jon
Lord's
retirement
from
the
band
in
2002
(being
succeeded
by
<a
href="/wiki/Don_Airey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Don
Airey">Don
Airey</a>)
left
Ian
Paice
as
the
only
original
Deep
Purple
member
still
in
the
band.</p>








<p>Deep
Purple
were
ranked
number
22
on
<a
href="/wiki/VH1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="VH1">VH1</a>'s
<i>Greatest
Artists
of
Hard
Rock</i>
programme<sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
a
British
radio
station
<a
href="/wiki/Planet_Rock_(radio_station)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Planet
Rock
(radio
station)">Planet
Rock</a>
poll
ranked
them
5th
among
the
&quot;most
influential
bands
ever&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
At
the
2011
<i><a
href="/wiki/Classic_Rock_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Classic
Rock
(magazine)">Classic
Rock</a></i>
Awards
in
London,
they
received
the
Innovator
Award.<sup
id="cite_ref-CRAward_17-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-CRAward-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
October
2012,
Deep
Purple
were
nominated
for
the
first
time
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame">Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame</a>,
but
were
not
voted
in
the
following
March.
In
October
2013,
the
band
was
announced
as
a
Hall
of
Fame
nominee
for
a
second
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-RS_2013_18-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RS_2013-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
style="overflow:hidden;height:;">

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="History">History</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Deep_Purple&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
History">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="The_beginning_.281967.E2.80.9368.29">The
beginning
(1967–68)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Deep_Purple&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
The
beginning
(1967–68)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
1967,
former
<a
href="/wiki/The_Searchers_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Searchers
(band)">Searchers</a>
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Chris_Curtis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chris
Curtis">Chris
Curtis</a>
contacted
London
businessman
Tony
Edwards,
in
the
hope
that
he
would
manage
a
new
group
he
was
putting
together,
to
be
called
<b>Roundabout</b>.
Curtis'
vision
was
a
&quot;supergroup&quot;
where
the
band
members
would
get
on
and
off,
like
a
musical
roundabout.
Impressed
with
the
plan,
Edwards
agreed
to
finance
the
venture
with
two
business
partners:
<a
href="/wiki/John_Coletta?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Coletta">John
Coletta</a>
and
Ron
Hire,
all
of
Hire-Edwards-Coletta
(HEC)
Enterprises.<sup
id="cite_ref-Thompson_19-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Thompson-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
first
recruit
was
the
classically-trained
<a
href="/wiki/Hammond_organ?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hammond
organ">Hammond
organ</a>
player
<a
href="/wiki/Jon_Lord?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jon
Lord">Jon
Lord</a>,
Curtis'
flatmate
who
had
most
notably
played
with
The
Artwoods
(led
by
<a
href="/wiki/Art_Wood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Art
Wood">Art
Wood</a>,
brother
of
future
Rolling
Stones
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Ronnie_Wood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ronnie
Wood">Ronnie
Wood</a>,
and
featuring
<a
href="/wiki/Keef_Hartley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Keef
Hartley">Keef
Hartley</a>).<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
was
followed
by
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Ritchie_Blackmore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ritchie
Blackmore">Ritchie
Blackmore</a>,
who
was
persuaded
to
return
from
<a
href="/wiki/Hamburg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>
to
audition
for
the
new
group.
Blackmore
was
making
a
name
for
himself
as
a
studio
session
guitarist,
and
had
also
been
a
member
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Outlaws_(UK_band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Outlaws
(UK
band)"
class="mw-redirect">The
Outlaws</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Screaming_Lord_Sutch?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Screaming
Lord
Sutch">Screaming
Lord
Sutch</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Neil_Christian?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Neil
Christian">Neil
Christian</a>.
Curtis'
erratic
behaviour
soon
forced
him
out
of
his
own
project,
but
Lord
and
Blackmore
were
keen
to
continue,
and
carried
on
recruiting
additional
members,
keeping
Tony
Edwards
as
their
manager.<sup
id="cite_ref-Curtis_21-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Curtis-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
class="quotebox"
style="float:
left;
clear:
left;
margin:
0.5em
1.4em
0.8em
0;
width:
33%;
padding:
6px;
border:
1px
solid
#aaa;
font-size:
88%;
background-color:
#F9F9F9;">









<div
style="position:
relative;
text-align:
left;">










<div
style="margin:0px
2em;">











<p>It
[&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Deep_Purple_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Deep
Purple
(song)">Deep
Purple</a>&quot;]
was
a
song
my
grandmother
used
to
play
on
the
piano</p>










</div>










<div
style="position:
absolute;
left:
0px;
top:
0px;
text-align:
left;
font-family:'Times
New
Roman',serif;
font-weight:bold;
font-size:
large;
color:
gray;">










“









</div>










<div
style="position:
absolute;
right:
0px;
bottom:
0px;
text-align:
left;
font-family:'Times
New
Roman',serif;
font-weight:bold;
font-size:
large;
color:
gray;">










”









</div>









</div>









<div
style="text-align:
left;">









—
Ritchie
Blackmore
on
choosing
the
band's
name.









<sup
id="cite_ref-Bloom_22-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Bloom-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>








</div>








</div>








<p>For
the
bass
guitar,
Lord
suggested
his
old
friend
<a
href="/wiki/Nick_Simper?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nick
Simper">Nick
Simper</a>,
with
whom
he
had
played
in
a
band
called
<a
href="/wiki/The_Flower_Pot_Men_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Flower
Pot
Men
(band)"
class="mw-redirect">The
Flower
Pot
Men
and
their
Garden</a>
(formerly
known
as
<a
href="/wiki/The_Ivy_League_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Ivy
League
(band)">The
Ivy
League</a>)
back
in
1967.
Simper
had
previously
been
in
<a
href="/wiki/Johnny_Kidd_and_the_Pirates?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Johnny
Kidd
and
the
Pirates"
class="mw-redirect">Johnny
Kidd
and
The
Pirates</a>
and
survived
the
car
crash
that
killed
Kidd.
Simper
had
known
Blackmore
since
the
early
1960s
when
his
first
band,
the
Renegades,
debuted
around
the
same
time
as
one
of
Blackmore's
early
bands,
the
Dominators.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Bobby_Woodman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bobby
Woodman"
class="mw-redirect">Bobby
Woodman</a>
was
the
initial
choice
for
the
drums,
but
during
the
auditions
for
a
singer,
<a
href="/wiki/Rod_Evans?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rod
Evans">Rod
Evans</a>
of
the
Maze
came
in
with
his
drummer,
<a
href="/wiki/Ian_Paice?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ian
Paice">Ian
Paice</a>.
Blackmore
had
seen
Paice
on
tour
with
the
Maze
in
Germany
in
1966,
and
had
been
impressed
by
the
18-year
old's
drumming.
While
Woodman
was
out
for
cigarettes,
Blackmore
quickly
arranged
an
audition
for
Paice.
Both
Paice
and
Evans
won
their
respective
jobs,
and
the
line-up
was
complete.<sup
id="cite_ref-autogenerated1983_24-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-autogenerated1983-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
band
began
in
earnest
in
March
1968
at
Deeves
Hall,
a
country
house
in
<a
href="/wiki/South_Mimms?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="South
Mimms">South
Mimms</a>,
Hertfordshire.<sup
id="cite_ref-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
would
live,
write
and
rehearse
at
Deeves
Hall,
which
was
fully
kitted
out
with
the
latest
<a
href="/wiki/Marshall_Amplification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Marshall
Amplification">Marshall</a>
amplification.<sup
id="cite_ref-Bloom_22-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Bloom-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
a
brief
tour
of
Denmark
and
Sweden
in
April,
in
which
they
were
still
billed
as
Roundabout,
Blackmore
suggested
a
new
name:
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Deep_Purple_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Deep
Purple
(song)">Deep
Purple</a>&quot;,
named
after
his
grandmother's
favourite
song.<sup
id="cite_ref-Curtis_21-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Curtis-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Bloom_22-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Bloom-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
group
had
resolved
to
choose
a
name
after
everyone
had
posted
one
on
a
board
in
rehearsal.
Second
to
Deep
Purple
was
&quot;Concrete
God&quot;,
which
the
band
thought
was
too
harsh
to
take
on.<sup
id="cite_ref-27"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Early_years_.281968.E2.80.9370.29">Early
years
(1968–70)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Deep_Purple&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
Early
years
(1968–70)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:182px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jon_Lord_1990.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Jon_Lord_1990.jpg/180px-Jon_Lord_1990.jpg"
width="180"
height="237"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Jon_Lord_1990.jpg/270px-Jon_Lord_1990.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/2/2c/Jon_Lord_1990.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jon_Lord_1990.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Organ
player











<a
href="/wiki/Jon_Lord?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jon
Lord">Jon
Lord</a>









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>In
May
1968,
the
band
moved
into
Pye
Studios
in
London's
<a
href="/wiki/Marble_Arch?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Marble
Arch">Marble
Arch</a>
to
record
their
debut
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Shades_of_Deep_Purple?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shades
of
Deep
Purple">Shades
of
Deep
Purple</a></i>,
which
was
released
in
July.<sup
id="cite_ref-Thompson2004_29-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Thompson2004-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
group
had
success
in
North
America
with
a
cover
of
<a
href="/wiki/Joe_South?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joe
South">Joe
South</a>'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Hush_(Billy_Joe_Royal_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hush
(Billy
Joe
Royal
song)">Hush</a>&quot;,
and
by
September
1968,
the
song
had
reached
number
4
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100">Billboard
Hot
100</a>
in
the
US
and
number
2
on
the
Canadian
<a
href="/wiki/RPM_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RPM
(magazine)">RPM</a>
charts,
pushing
the
<i>Shades</i>
LP
up
to
No.&nbsp;24
on
Billboard's
pop
album
charts.<sup
id="cite_ref-Miles_30-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Miles-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
following
month,
Deep
Purple
was
booked
to
support
<a
href="/wiki/Cream_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cream
(band)">Cream</a>
on
their
<i><a
href="/wiki/Goodbye_(Cream_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Goodbye
(Cream
album)">Goodbye</a></i>
tour.<sup
id="cite_ref-Miles_30-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Miles-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
band's
second
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Book_of_Taliesyn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Book
of
Taliesyn">The
Book
of
Taliesyn</a></i>
(including
a
cover
of
<a
href="/wiki/Neil_Diamond?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Neil
Diamond">Neil
Diamond</a>'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Kentucky_Woman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kentucky
Woman">Kentucky
Woman</a>&quot;),
was
released
in
North
America
to
coincide
with
the
tour,
reaching
number
38
on
the
Billboard
charts
and
number
21
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/RPM_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RPM
(magazine)">RPM</a>
charts,
although
it
would
not
be
released
in
their
home
country
until
the
following
year.
Early
1969
saw
Deep
Purple
record
their
third
album,
simply
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Deep_Purple_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Deep
Purple
(album)">Deep
Purple</a></i>.
The
album
contained
strings
and
woodwind
on
one
track
(&quot;April&quot;),
showcasing
Lord's
classical
antecedents
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Johann
Sebastian
Bach">Bach</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Nikolai_Rimsky-Korsakov?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nikolai
Rimsky-Korsakov">Rimsky-Korsakov</a>,
and
several
other
influences
were
in
evidence,
notably
<a
href="/wiki/Vanilla_Fudge?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vanilla
Fudge">Vanilla
Fudge</a>.
(Lord
and
Blackmore
had
even
claimed
the
group
wanted
to
be
a
&quot;Vanilla
Fudge
clone&quot;.)<sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
Not
satisfied
with
the
possibilities
for
singles
off
this
album,
the
band
also
recorded
a
single
called
&quot;Emmaretta&quot;,
named
after
Emmaretta
Marks,
then
a
cast
member
of
the
musical
<i><a
href="/wiki/Hair_(musical)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hair
(musical)">Hair</a></i>,
whom
Evans
was
trying
to
seduce.
This
would
be
the
last
recording
by
the
original
line-up.<sup
id="cite_ref-33"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Deep
Purple's
troubled
North
American
record
label,
Tetragrammaton,
delayed
production
of
the
<i>Deep
Purple</i>
album
until
after
the
band's
1969
American
tour
ended.
This,
as
well
as
lackluster
promotion
by
the
nearly-broke
label,
caused
the
album
to
sell
poorly,
finishing
well
out
of
the
Billboard
Top
100.
Soon
after
the
third
album's
eventual
release,
Tetragrammaton
went
out
of
business,
leaving
the
band
with
no
money
and
an
uncertain
future.
(Tetragrammaton's
assets
were
assumed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Warner
Bros.
Records">Warner
Bros.
Records</a>,
who
would
release
Deep
Purple's
records
in
the
US
throughout
the
1970s.)
During
the
1969
American
tour,
Lord
and
Blackmore
met
with
Paice
to
discuss
their
desire
to
take
the
band
in
a
heavier
direction.
Feeling
that
Evans
and
Simper
would
not
fit
well
with
a
heavy
rock
style,
both
were
replaced
that
summer.<sup
id="cite_ref-34"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
Paice
stated,
&quot;A
change
had
to
come.
If
they
hadn't
left,
the
band
would
have
totally
disintegrated.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-autogenerated1983_24-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-autogenerated1983-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
As
Ritchie
Blackmore
explained
it:</p>








<blockquote>









<p>Nicky
wasn’t
constructive,
he
didn’t
have
any
ideas,
and
he
was
an
average
bass
player,
so
he
had
to
go.
Rod
just
wanted
to
go
to
America
and
live
in
America.<sup
id="cite_ref-Rosen_Interview_1_35-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rosen_Interview_1-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








</blockquote>








<div
class="thumb
tleft">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:172px;">









<a

1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Deep_Purple%2C_Ritchie_Blackmore_1970.jpg/340px-Deep_Purple%2C_Ritchie_Blackmore_1970.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Deep_Purple,_Ritchie_Blackmore_1970.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>











<a
href="/wiki/Ritchie_Blackmore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ritchie
Blackmore">Ritchie
Blackmore</a>
in
Hannover,
Germany,
1970









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>In
search
of
a
replacement
vocalist,
Blackmore
set
his
own
sights
on
19-year-old
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Terry_Reid?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Terry
Reid">Terry
Reid</a>.
Though
he
found
the
offer
&quot;flattering&quot;,
Reid
was
still
bound
by
the
exclusive
recording
contract
with
his
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Mickie_Most?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mickie
Most">Mickie
Most</a>
and
more
interested
in
his
solo
career.<sup
id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>
Blackmore
had
no
other
choice
but
to
look
elsewhere.
The
band
hunted
down
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Ian_Gillan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ian
Gillan">Ian
Gillan</a>
from
<a
href="/wiki/Episode_Six?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Episode
Six">Episode
Six</a>,
a
band
that
had
released
several
singles
in
the
UK
without
achieving
their
big
break
for
commercial
success.
Gillan
had
at
one
time
been
approached
by
Nick
Simper
when
Deep
Purple
was
first
forming,
but
Gillan
had
reportedly
told
Simper
that
the
Roundabout
project
would
not
go
anywhere,
while
he
felt
Episode
Six
was
poised
to
make
it
big.<sup
id="cite_ref-37"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
Six's
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Mick_Underwood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mick
Underwood">Mick
Underwood</a>
–
an
old
comrade
of
Blackmore's
from
his
days
in
<a
href="/wiki/The_Outlaws_(UK_band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Outlaws
(UK
band)"
class="mw-redirect">The
Outlaws</a>
–
introduced
the
band
to
Gillan
and
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Roger_Glover?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roger
Glover">Roger
Glover</a>.
This
effectively
killed
Episode
Six
and
gave
Underwood
a
guilt
complex
that
lasted
nearly
a
decade,
until
Gillan
recruited
him
for
<a
href="/wiki/Gillan_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gillan
(band)">his
new
post-Purple
band</a>
in
the
late
1970s.
According
to
Blackmore,
Deep
Purple
was
only
interested
in
Gillan
and
not
Glover,
but
Roger
was
retained
on
the
advice
of
Ian
Paice.</p>








<div
class="quotebox"
style="float:
right;
clear:
right;
margin:
0.5em
0
0.8em
1.4em;

solid

#F9F9F9;">

style="position:

text-align:

<div
style="margin:0px
2em;">











<p>He
turned
up
for
the
session...he
was
their
[Episode
Six's]
bass
player.
We
weren’t
originally
going
to
take
him
until
Paicey
said,
“he’s
a
good
bass
player,
let’s
keep
him.”
So
I
said
okay.</p>










</div>










<div
style="position:
absolute;
left:
0px;
top:
0px;
text-align:
left;
font-family:'Times
New
Roman',serif;
font-weight:bold;
font-size:
large;
color:
gray;">










“









</div>










<div
style="position:
absolute;
right:
0px;
bottom:
0px;
text-align:
left;
font-family:'Times
New
Roman',serif;
font-weight:bold;
font-size:
large;
color:
gray;">










”









</div>









</div>









<div
style="text-align:
left;">









—
Ritchie
Blackmore
on
the
hiring
of
Roger
Glover.









<sup
id="cite_ref-Rosen_Interview_1_35-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rosen_Interview_1-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>








</div>








</div>








<p>This
created
the
Deep
Purple
Mark
II
line-up,
whose
first
release
was
a
<a
href="/wiki/Roger_Greenaway?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roger
Greenaway">Greenaway</a>-<a
href="/wiki/Roger_Cook_(songwriter)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roger
Cook
(songwriter)">Cook</a>
tune
titled
&quot;Hallelujah&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Hallelujah_38-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Hallelujah-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup>
Despite
TV
appearances
to
promote
the
record
in
the
UK,
the
song
flopped.<sup
id="cite_ref-Hallelujah_38-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Hallelujah-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup>
Blackmore
had
told
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Record_Mirror?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Record
Mirror">Record
Mirror</a></i>
they
&quot;need
to
have
a
commercial
record
in
Britain&quot;,
and
described
the
song
as
&quot;an
in-between
sort
of
thing&quot;—a
median
between
what
the
band
would
normally
make
but
with
an
added
commercial
motive.<sup
id="cite_ref-Hallelujah_38-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Hallelujah-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
band
gained
some
much-needed
publicity
in
September
1969,
with
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Concerto_for_Group_and_Orchestra?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Concerto
for
Group
and
Orchestra">Concerto
for
Group
and
Orchestra</a></i>,
a
three-movement
epic
composed
by
Lord
as
a
solo
project
and
performed
by
the
band
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Royal
Albert
Hall">Royal
Albert
Hall</a>
with
the
<a
href="/wiki/Royal_Philharmonic_Orchestra?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Royal
Philharmonic
Orchestra">Royal
Philharmonic
Orchestra</a>,
conducted
by
<a
href="/wiki/Malcolm_Arnold?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Malcolm
Arnold">Malcolm
Arnold</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Miles_30-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Miles-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
Together
with
<i><a
href="/wiki/Five_Bridges?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Five
Bridges">Five
Bridges</a></i>
by
<a
href="/wiki/The_Nice?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Nice">The
Nice</a>,
it
was
one
of
the
first
collaborations
between
a
rock
band
and
an
orchestra.
This
live
album
became
their
first
album
with
any
kind
of
chart
success
in
the
UK.<sup
id="cite_ref-39"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
Gillan
and
Blackmore
especially
were
less
than
happy
at
the
band
being
tagged
as
&quot;a
group
who
played
with
orchestras&quot;
at
the
time;
what
they
had
in
mind
was
to
develop
the
band
into
a
much
tighter,
hard-rocking
style.
Despite
this,
Lord
wrote
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Gemini_Suite_Live?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gemini
Suite
Live">Gemini
Suite</a></i>,
another
orchestra/group
collaboration
in
the
same
vein,
for
the
band
in
late
1970.
In
1975,
Blackmore
stated
that
he
thought
the
<i>Concerto
for
Group
and
Orchestra</i>
wasn’t
bad
but
the
<i>Gemini
Suite</i>
was
horrible
and
very
disjointed.<sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
Roger
Glover
later
claimed
Jon
Lord
had
appeared
to
be
the
leader
of
the
band
in
the
early
years.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
style="clear:both;"></div>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Breakthrough_success_.281970.E2.80.9373.29">Breakthrough
success
(1970–73)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Deep_Purple&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
Breakthrough
success
(1970–73)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:202px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ian_Gillan_(1972).jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Ian_Gillan_%281972%29.jpg/200px-Ian_Gillan_%281972%29.jpg"
width="200"
height="278"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Ian_Gillan_%281972%29.jpg/300px-Ian_Gillan_%281972%29.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/1/1d/Ian_Gillan_%281972%29.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ian_Gillan_(1972).jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Vocalist











<a
href="/wiki/Ian_Gillan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ian
Gillan">Ian
Gillan</a>
on
stage
in
Clemson,
South
Carolina,
US,
1972









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Shortly
after
the
orchestral
release,
Deep
Purple
began
a
hectic
touring
and
recording
schedule
that
was
to
see
little
respite
for
the
next
three
years.
Their
first
studio
album
of
this
period,
released
in
mid-1970,
was
<i><a
href="/wiki/Deep_Purple_in_Rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Deep
Purple
in
Rock">In
Rock</a></i>
(a
name
supported
by
the
album's
<a
href="/wiki/Mount_Rushmore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mount
Rushmore">Mount
Rushmore</a>-inspired
cover),
which
contained
the
then-concert
staples
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Speed_King?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Speed
King">Speed
King</a>&quot;,
&quot;Into
The
Fire&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Child_in_Time?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Child
in
Time">Child
in
Time</a>&quot;.
The
band
also
issued
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Black_Night?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Night">Black
Night</a>&quot;,
which
finally
put
Deep
Purple
into
the
UK
Top
Ten.<sup
id="cite_ref-Roberts_42-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Roberts-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
interplay
between
Blackmore's
guitar
and
Lord's
distorted
organ,
coupled
with
Gillan's
howling
vocals
and
the
rhythm
section
of
Glover
and
Paice,
now
started
to
take
on
a
unique
identity
that
further
separated
the
band
from
its
earlier
albums.
Along
with
Zeppelin's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin_II?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Led
Zeppelin
II">Led
Zeppelin
II</a></i>
and
Sabbath's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Paranoid_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paranoid
(album)">Paranoid</a></i>,
<i>In
Rock</i>
codified
the
<a
href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Heavy
metal
music">heavy
metal</a>
genre.<sup
id="cite_ref-Wasler_2-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Wasler-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
the
album's
development,
Blackmore
stated:</p>








<blockquote>









<p>I
got
fed
up
with
playing
with
classical
orchestras,
and
thought,
&quot;well,
this
is
my
turn.&quot;
Jon
was
into
more
classical.
I
thought,
&quot;well
you
do
that,
I'll
do
rock.&quot;
And
I
said,
&quot;If
this
fails,
this
record,
I'll
play
with
orchestras
the
rest
of
my
life.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-43"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








</blockquote>








<p><i>In
Rock</i>
performed
well,
especially
in
the
UK
where
it
reached
#4,
while
the
&quot;Black
Night&quot;
single
reached
#2,
and
the
band
performed
the
song
live
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/BBC?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BBC">BBC</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/Top_of_the_Pops?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Top
of
the
Pops">Top
of
the
Pops</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-44"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>A
second
album,
the
creatively
progressive
<i><a
href="/wiki/Fireball_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fireball
(album)">Fireball</a></i>,
was
issued
in
the
summer
of
1971.
The
title
track
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Fireball_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fireball
(song)">Fireball</a>&quot;
was
released
as
a
single,
as
was
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Strange_Kind_of_Woman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Strange
Kind
of
Woman">Strange
Kind
of
Woman</a>&quot;,
not
from
the
album
but
recorded
during
the
same
sessions
(although
it
replaced
&quot;Demon's
Eye&quot;
on
the
US
version
of
the
album).<sup
id="cite_ref-45"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Within
weeks
of
<i>Fireball'</i>s
release,
the
band
were
already
performing
songs
planned
for
the
next
album.
One
song
(which
later
became
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Highway_Star_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Highway
Star
(song)">Highway
Star</a>&quot;)
was
performed
at
the
first
gig
of
the
<i>Fireball</i>
tour,
having
been
written
on
the
bus
to
a
show
in
Portsmouth,
in
answer
to
a
journalist's
question:
&quot;How
do
you
go
about
writing
songs?&quot;
Three
months
later,
in
December
1971,
the
band
travelled
to
Switzerland
to
record
<i><a
href="/wiki/Machine_Head_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Machine
Head
(album)">Machine
Head</a></i>.
The
album
was
due
to
be
recorded
at
a
casino
in
<a
href="/wiki/Montreux?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Montreux">Montreux</a>,
using
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stones_Mobile_Studio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stones
Mobile
Studio">Rolling
Stones
Mobile
Studio</a>,
but
a
fire
during
a
<a
href="/wiki/Frank_Zappa?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Frank
Zappa">Frank
Zappa</a>
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Mothers_of_Invention?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mothers
of
Invention"
class="mw-redirect">Mothers
of
Invention</a>
gig,
caused
by
a
man
firing
a
flare
gun
into
the
ceiling,
burned
down
the
casino.
This
incident
famously
inspired
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Smoke_on_the_Water?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Smoke
on
the
Water">Smoke
on
the
Water</a>&quot;.
The
album
was
later
recorded
in
a
corridor
at
the
nearby
empty
Grand
Hotel.<sup
id="cite_ref-46"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-47"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Continuing
from
where
both
previous
albums
left
off,
<i>Machine
Head</i>
became
one
of
the
band's
most
famous
albums.
It
reached
number
1
in
the
UK,
while
re-establishing
Deep
Purple
in
North
America,
hitting
number
7
in
the
U.S.
and
number
1
in
Canada.
It
included
tracks
that
became
live
classics,
such
as
&quot;Highway
Star&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Space_Truckin%27?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Space
Truckin'">Space
Truckin'</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lazy_(Deep_Purple_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lazy
(Deep
Purple
song)">Lazy</a>&quot;
and
&quot;Smoke
on
the
Water&quot;,
for
which
Deep
Purple
is
most
famous.<sup
id="cite_ref-Roberts_42-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Roberts-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-48"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup>
Deep
Purple
continued
to
tour
and
record
at
a
rate
that
would
be
rare
thirty
years
on;
when
<i>Machine
Head</i>
was
recorded,
the
group
had
only
been
together
three
and
a
half
years,
yet
the
album
was
their
sixth.</p>








<div
class="quotebox"
style="float:
right;
clear:
right;
margin:
0.5em
0
0.8em
1.4em;
width:
33%;
padding:
6px;
border:
1px
solid
#aaa;
font-size:
88%;
background-color:
#F9F9F9;">









<div
style="position:
relative;
text-align:
left;">










<div
style="margin:0px
2em;">











<p>When
I
was
nine
years
old
it
was
all
about
Deep
Purple.
My
all
time
favourite
[album]
is
still
<i><a
href="/wiki/Made_in_Japan_(Deep_Purple_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Made
in
Japan
(Deep
Purple
album)">Made
in
Japan</a></i></p>










</div>










<div
style="position:
absolute;
left:
0px;
top:
0px;
text-align:
left;
font-family:'Times
New
Roman',serif;
font-weight:bold;
font-size:
large;
color:
gray;">










“









</div>










<div
style="position:
absolute;
right:
0px;
bottom:
0px;
text-align:
left;
font-family:'Times
New
Roman',serif;
font-weight:bold;
font-size:
large;
color:
gray;">










”









</div>









</div>









<div
style="text-align:
left;">









—
Metallica
drummer










<a
href="/wiki/Lars_Ulrich?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lars
Ulrich">Lars
Ulrich</a>.









<sup
id="cite_ref-49"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup>








</div>








</div>








<p>Meanwhile,
the
band
undertook
four
North
America
tours
in
1972,
and
a
Japan
tour
that
led
to
a
double-vinyl
live
release,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Made_in_Japan_(Deep_Purple_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Made
in
Japan
(Deep
Purple
album)">Made
in
Japan</a></i>.
Originally
intended
as
a
Japan-only
record,
its
worldwide
release
saw
the
double
LP
become
an
instant
hit.
It
remains
one
of
rock
music's
most
popular
and
highest
selling
live-concert
recordings.<sup
id="cite_ref-Made_in_Japan_50-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Made_in_Japan-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
classic
Deep
Purple
Mark
II
line-up
continued
to
work,
and
released
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Who_Do_We_Think_We_Are?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Who
Do
We
Think
We
Are">Who
Do
We
Think
We
Are</a></i>
in
1973.
Featuring
the
hit
single
&quot;Woman
from
Tokyo&quot;,
the
album
performed
well,
hitting
number
4
in
the
UK
charts
and
number
15
in
the
US
charts
while
achieving
gold
record
status
faster
than
any
Deep
Purple
album
released
up
to
that
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-51"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-52"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup>
But
internal
tensions
and
exhaustion
were
more
noticeable
than
ever.
In
many
ways,
the
band
had
become
victims
of
their
own
success.
Following
the
successes
of
<i>Machine
Head</i>
and
<i>Made
in
Japan</i>,
the
addition
of
<i>Who
Do
We
Think
We
Are</i>
made
them
the
top-selling
artists
of
1973
in
the
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-53"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-54"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="New_line-up.2C_successes_and_struggles_.281973-76.29">New
line-up,
successes
and
struggles
(1973-76)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Deep_Purple&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
New
line-up,
successes
and
struggles
(1973-76)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Ian
Gillan
admitted
in
a
1984
interview
that
the
band
was
pushed
by
management
to
complete
the
<i>Who
Do
We
Think
We
Are</i>
album
on
time
and
go
on
tour,
although
they
badly
needed
a
break.<sup
id="cite_ref-55"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
bad
feelings
culminated
in
Gillan,
followed
by
Glover,
quitting
the
band
after
their
second
tour
of
Japan
in
the
summer
of
1973
over
tensions
with
Blackmore.<sup
id="cite_ref-56"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-57"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-58"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:202px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:David_Coverdale_1.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/David_Coverdale_1.jpg/200px-David_Coverdale_1.jpg"
width="200"
height="266"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/David_Coverdale_1.jpg/300px-David_Coverdale_1.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/David_Coverdale_1.jpg/400px-David_Coverdale_1.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:David_Coverdale_1.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
David
Coverdale,
vocalist
between
August
1973
and
March
1976









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>The
band
first
hired
Midlands
bassist/vocalist
<a
href="/wiki/Glenn_Hughes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glenn
Hughes">Glenn
Hughes</a>,
formerly
of
<a
href="/wiki/Trapeze_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Trapeze
(band)">Trapeze</a>.
According
to
Ian
Paice,
Glover
had
told
him
and
Lord
a
few
months
before
his
official
resignation
that
he
wanted
to
leave
the
band,
so
they
had
already
started
to
drop
in
on
Trapeze
shows.
After
acquiring
Hughes,
they
debated
continuing
as
a
four-piece
band,
with
Hughes
as
both
bassist
and
lead
vocalist.<sup
id="cite_ref-59"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-vanderlee_60-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-vanderlee-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup>
According
to
Hughes,
he
was
persuaded
to
join
under
the
guise
that
the
band
would
be
bringing
in
<a
href="/wiki/Paul_Rodgers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paul
Rodgers">Paul
Rodgers</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Free_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Free
(band)">Free</a>
as
a
co-lead
vocalist,
but
by
that
time
Rodgers
had
just
started
<a
href="/wiki/Bad_Company?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bad
Company">Bad
Company</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-61"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup>
Instead,
auditions
were
held
for
lead
vocal
replacements.
They
settled
on
<a
href="/wiki/David_Coverdale?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Coverdale">David
Coverdale</a>,
an
unknown
singer
from
<a
href="/wiki/Saltburn-by-the-Sea?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Saltburn-by-the-Sea">Saltburn</a>
in
Northeast
England,
primarily
because
Blackmore
liked
his
masculine,
blues-tinged
voice.<sup
id="cite_ref-vanderlee_60-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-vanderlee-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>This
new
line-up
continued
into
1974,
and
their
spring
tour
included
shows
at
<a
href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madison
Square
Garden">Madison
Square
Garden</a>,
New
York
on
13
March,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Nassau_Coliseum?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nassau
Coliseum"
class="mw-redirect">Nassau
Coliseum</a>
four
days
later.<sup
id="cite_ref-62"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
then
headlined
the
famous
<a
href="/wiki/California_Jam?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="California
Jam">California
Jam</a>
festival
at
<a
href="/wiki/Ontario_Motor_Speedway?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ontario
Motor
Speedway">Ontario
Motor
Speedway</a>
located
in
<a
href="/wiki/Ontario,_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ontario,
California">Southern
California</a>
on
6
April
1974.
Attracting
over
250,000<sup
id="cite_ref-63"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup>
fans,
the
festival
also
included
1970s
rock
giants
<a
href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Sabbath">Black
Sabbath</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Eagles_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eagles
(band)">Eagles</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Emerson,_Lake_%26_Palmer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Emerson,
Lake
&amp;
Palmer">Emerson,
Lake
&amp;
Palmer</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Earth,_Wind_%26_Fire?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Earth,
Wind
&amp;
Fire">Earth,
Wind
&amp;
Fire</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Seals_and_Crofts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Seals
and
Crofts">Seals
and
Crofts</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Rare_Earth_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rare
Earth
(band)">Rare
Earth</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Black_Oak_Arkansas?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Oak
Arkansas">Black
Oak
Arkansas</a>.
Portions
of
the
show
were
telecast
on
<a
href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Broadcasting
Company">ABC</a>
Television
in
the
US,
exposing
the
band
to
a
wider
audience.
This
line-up's
first
album,
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Burn_(Deep_Purple_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Burn
(Deep
Purple
album)">Burn</a></i>,
was
a
highly
successful
release
(only
the
second
studio
album,
after
<i>Machine
Head</i>,
to
crack
the
US
Top
10),
and
was
followed
by
another
world
tour.
The
title
track
&quot;Burn&quot;,
which
opens
the
album,
was
a
conscious
effort
by
the
band
to
embrace
the
progressive
rock
movement
that
was
popularized
at
the
time
by
bands
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Yes_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Yes
(band)">Yes</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Emerson,_Lake_%26_Palmer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Emerson,
Lake
&amp;
Palmer">ELP</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Genesis_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Genesis
(band)">Genesis</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Gentle_Giant?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gentle
Giant">Gentle
Giant</a>,
etc.
&quot;Burn&quot;
was
a
complex
arrangement
which
showcased
all
the
band
members'
musical
virtuosity
and
particularly
Blackmore's
classically-influenced
guitar
prowess.
The
album
also
featured
Hughes
and
Coverdale
providing
vocal
harmonies
and
elements
of
funk
and
blues,
respectively,
to
the
band's
music,
a
sound
that
was
even
more
apparent
on
the
late
1974
release
<i><a
href="/wiki/Stormbringer_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stormbringer
(album)">Stormbringer</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-vanderlee_60-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-vanderlee-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup>
Besides
the
title
track,
the
<i>Stormbringer</i>
album
had
a
number
of
songs
that
received
much
radio
play,
such
as
&quot;Lady
Double
Dealer&quot;,
&quot;The
Gypsy&quot;
and
&quot;Soldier
Of
Fortune.&quot;
However,
Blackmore
publicly
disliked
the
album
and
the
funky
soul
elements,
even
calling
it
&quot;shoeshine
music&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-64"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-65"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-66"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup>
As
a
result,
he
left
the
band
on
21
June
1975
to
form
his
own
band
with
<a
href="/wiki/Ronnie_James_Dio?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ronnie
James
Dio">Ronnie
James
Dio</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Elf_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Elf
(band)">Elf</a>,
called
Ritchie
Blackmore's
Rainbow,
later
shortened
to
<a
href="/wiki/Rainbow_(English_band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rainbow
(English
band)"
class="mw-redirect">Rainbow</a>
after
one
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-67"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
class="thumb
tleft">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:204px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Glenn_hughes.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/9/9c/Glenn_hughes.jpg"
width="202"
height="233"
class="thumbimage"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Glenn_hughes.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Glenn
Hughes,
bassist
and
co-lead
vocalist
with
Coverdale,
1973
to
1976









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>With
Blackmore's
departure,
Deep
Purple
was
left
to
fill
one
of
the
biggest
band
member
vacancies
in
rock
music.
In
spite
of
this,
the
rest
of
the
band
refused
to
stop,
and
announced
a
replacement
for
Blackmore:
American
<a
href="/wiki/Tommy_Bolin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tommy
Bolin">Tommy
Bolin</a>.
Before
Bolin
was
recruited,
<a
href="/wiki/Clem_Clempson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Clem
Clempson">Clem
Clempson</a>
(Colosseum,
Humble
Pie),
<a
href="/wiki/Zal_Cleminson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Zal
Cleminson">Zal
Cleminson</a>
(The
Sensational
Alex
Harvey
Band),
<a
href="/wiki/Mick_Ronson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mick
Ronson">Mick
Ronson</a>
(David
Bowie
&amp;
The
Spiders
From
Mars)
and
<a
href="/wiki/Rory_Gallagher?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rory
Gallagher">Rory
Gallagher</a>
were
considered
for
the
part.<sup
id="cite_ref-68"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>There
are
at
least
two
versions
about
the
recruitment
of
Bolin:
Coverdale
claims
to
have
been
the
one
who
suggested
auditioning
Bolin.<sup
id="cite_ref-69"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;He
walked
in,
thin
as
a
rake,
his
hair
coloured
green,
yellow
and
blue
with
feathers
in
it.
Slinking
along
beside
him
was
this
stunning
Hawaiian
girl
in
a
crochet
dress
with
nothing
on
underneath.
He
plugged
into
four
<a
href="/wiki/Marshall_Amplification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Marshall
Amplification">Marshall</a>
100-watt
stacks
and...the
job
was
his&quot;.
But
in
an
interview
originally
published
by
Melody
Maker
in
June
1975,
Bolin
himself
claimed
that
he
came
to
the
audition
following
a
recommendation
from
Blackmore.<sup
id="cite_ref-70"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bolin
had
been
a
member
of
many
now-forgotten
late-1960s
bands
–
Denny
&amp;
The
Triumphs,
American
Standard,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Zephyr_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Zephyr
(band)">Zephyr</a>,
which
released
three
albums
from
1969–72.
Before
Deep
Purple,
Bolin's
best-known
recordings
were
made
as
a
session
musician
on
<a
href="/wiki/Billy_Cobham?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billy
Cobham">Billy
Cobham</a>'s
1973
<a
href="/wiki/Jazz_fusion?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jazz
fusion">jazz
fusion</a>
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Spectrum_(Billy_Cobham_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Spectrum
(Billy
Cobham
album)">Spectrum</a></i>,
and
as
lead
guitarist
on
two
post-<a
href="/wiki/Joe_Walsh?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joe
Walsh">Joe
Walsh</a>
<a
href="/wiki/James_Gang?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="James
Gang">James
Gang</a>
albums:
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bang_(James_Gang_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bang
(James
Gang
album)">Bang</a></i>
(1973)
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Miami_(James_Gang_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Miami
(James
Gang
album)">Miami</a></i>
(1974).
He
had
also
jammed
with
such
luminaries
as
Dr.
John,
Albert
King,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Good_Rats?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Good
Rats">The
Good
Rats</a>,
Moxy
and
<a
href="/wiki/Alphonse_Mouzon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alphonse
Mouzon">Alphonse
Mouzon</a>,
and
was
busy
working
on
his
first
solo
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Teaser_(Tommy_Bolin_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Teaser
(Tommy
Bolin
album)">Teaser</a></i>,
when
he
accepted
the
invitation
to
join
Deep
Purple.<sup
id="cite_ref-Talevski_71-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Talevski-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
resulting
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Come_Taste_the_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Come
Taste
the
Band">Come
Taste
the
Band</a></i>,
was
released
in
October
1975,
one
month
before
Bolin's
<i>Teaser</i>
album.
Despite
mixed
reviews
and
so-so
sales
(#19
on
the
U.K.
charts
and
#43
on
the
U.S.
Billboard
charts),
the
collection
revitalised
the
band
once
again,
bringing
a
new,
extreme
funk
edge
to
their
<a
href="/wiki/Hard_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hard
rock">hard
rock</a>
sound.<sup
id="cite_ref-bbc_72-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bbc-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bolin's
influence
was
crucial,
and
with
encouragement
from
Hughes
and
Coverdale,
the
guitarist
developed
much
of
the
album's
material.
Later,
Bolin's
personal
problems
with
drugs
began
to
manifest
themselves,
and
after
cancelled
shows
and
below-par
concert
performances,
the
band
was
in
danger.</p>








<div
style="clear:both;"></div>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Band_split_and_solo_projects_.281976.E2.80.9384.29">Band
split
and
solo
projects
(1976–84)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Deep_Purple&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
Band
split
and
solo
projects
(1976–84)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:182px;">









<a
href="/wiki?title=Special:Upload&amp;wpDestFile=TommyBolin.jpg"
class="new"
title="File:TommyBolin.jpg">File:TommyBolin.jpg</a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">










Tommy
Bolin,
guitarist
from
1975-76,
in
a
promo
photo









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>The
end
came
on
tour
in
England
on
15
March
1976
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Liverpool_Empire_Theatre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Liverpool
Empire
Theatre">Liverpool
Empire
Theatre</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-73"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup>
Coverdale
reportedly
walked
off
in
tears
and
handed
in
his
resignation,
to
which
he
was
allegedly
told
there
was
no
band
left
to
quit.
The
decision
to
disband
Deep
Purple
had
been
made
some
time
before
the
last
show
by
Lord
and
Paice
(the
last
remaining
original
members),
who
hadn't
told
anyone
else.
The
break-up
was
finally
made
public
in
July
1976.<sup
id="cite_ref-74"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Later,
Bolin
had
just
finished
recording
his
second
solo
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Private_Eyes_(Tommy_Bolin_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Private
Eyes
(Tommy
Bolin
album)">Private
Eyes</a></i>,
when,
on
4
December
1976,
tragedy
struck.<sup
id="cite_ref-Talevski_71-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Talevski-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
Miami,
during
a
tour
supporting
<a
href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jeff
Beck">Jeff
Beck</a>,
Bolin
was
found
unconscious
by
his
girlfriend
and
bandmates.
Unable
to
wake
him,
she
hurriedly
called
paramedics,
but
it
was
too
late.
The
official
cause
of
death
was
multiple-drug
intoxication.
Bolin
was
25
years
old.<sup
id="cite_ref-Talevski_71-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Talevski-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>After
the
break-up,
most
of
the
past
and
present
members
of
Deep
Purple
went
on
to
have
considerable
success
in
a
number
of
other
bands,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Gillan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gillan">Gillan</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Whitesnake?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Whitesnake">Whitesnake</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Rainbow_(English_band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rainbow
(English
band)"
class="mw-redirect">Rainbow</a>.
There
were,
however,
a
number
of
promoter-led
attempts
to
get
the
band
to
reform,
especially
with
the
revival
of
the
hard
rock
market
in
the
late
1970s
and
early
1980s.
In
1980,
a
touring
version
of
the
band
surfaced
with
Rod
Evans
as
the
only
member
who
had
ever
been
in
Deep
Purple,
eventually
ending
in
successful
legal
action
from
the
legitimate
Deep
Purple
camp
over
unauthorised
use
of
the
name.
Evans
was
ordered
to
pay
damages
of
US$672,000
for
using
the
band
name
without
permission.<sup
id="cite_ref-75"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Reformation.2C_reunions_and_turmoil_.281984.E2.80.9394.29">Reformation,
reunions
and
turmoil
(1984–94)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Deep_Purple&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"
title="Edit
section:
Reformation,
reunions
and
turmoil
(1984–94)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
April
1984,
eight
years
after
the
demise
of
Deep
Purple,
a
full-scale
(and
legal)
reunion
took
place
with
the
&quot;classic&quot;
early
1970s
line-up
of
Gillan,
Lord,
Blackmore,
Glover
and
Paice.<sup
id="cite_ref-76"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-77"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
reformed
band
signed
a
worldwide
deal
with
<a
href="/wiki/PolyGram?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="PolyGram">PolyGram</a>,
with
<a
href="/wiki/Mercury_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mercury
Records">Mercury
Records</a>
releasing
their
albums
in
the
US,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Polydor_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Polydor
Records">Polydor
Records</a>
in
the
UK
and
other
countries.
The
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Perfect_Strangers_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Perfect
Strangers
(album)">Perfect
Strangers</a></i>
was
recorded
in
Vermont
and
released
in
October
1984.
A
solid
release,
it
sold
extremely
well
(reaching
number
5
in
the
UK<sup
id="cite_ref-Roberts_42-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Roberts-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
number
17
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200">Billboard
200</a>
in
the
US<sup
id="cite_ref-AllMusic.com_78-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AllMusic.com-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup>)
and
included
the
singles
and
concert
staples
&quot;Knockin'
At
Your
Back
Door&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Perfect_Strangers_(Deep_Purple_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Perfect
Strangers
(Deep
Purple
song)">Perfect
Strangers</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-79"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
reunion
tour
followed,
starting
in
Australia
and
winding
its
way
across
the
world
to
North
America,
then
into
Europe
by
the
following
summer.
Financially,
the
tour
was
also
a
tremendous
success.
In
the
U.S.,
the
1985
tour
out-grossed
every
other
artist
except
<a
href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bruce
Springsteen">Bruce
Springsteen</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-80"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
UK
homecoming
saw
the
band
perform
a
<a
href="/wiki/Concerts_at_Knebworth_House?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Concerts
at
Knebworth
House">concert
at
Knebworth</a>
on
22
June
1985
(with
main
support
from
the
<a
href="/wiki/Scorpions_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scorpions
(band)">Scorpions</a>;
also
on
the
bill
were
<a
href="/wiki/UFO_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UFO
(band)">UFO</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Meat_Loaf?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Meat
Loaf">Meat
Loaf</a>),
where
the
weather
was
bad
(torrential
rain
and
6&quot;
of
mud)
in
front
of
80,000
fans.<sup
id="cite_ref-81"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
gig
was
called
the
&quot;Return
Of
The
Knebworth
Fayre&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-82"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
class="thumb
tleft">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:202px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Deep_Purple_(1985).jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
